					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">American rapper and record producer (1992–2018)</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with the cross-country skier <a href="/wiki/Mack_Miller" title="Mack Miller">Mack Miller</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">


</p>

<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://macmillerswebsite.com">macmillerswebsite<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Malcolm James McCormick</b> (January 19, 1992 – September 7, 2018), known professionally as <b>Mac Miller</b>, was an American rapper and record producer. Miller began his career in Pittsburgh's <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" class="mw-redirect" title="Hip hop">hip hop</a> scene in 2007, at the age of fifteen. In 2010, he signed a record deal with independent label <a href="/wiki/Rostrum_Records" title="Rostrum Records">Rostrum Records</a> and released his breakthrough <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtapes</a> <i><a href="/wiki/K.I.D.S._(mixtape)" class="mw-redirect" title="K.I.D.S. (mixtape)">K.I.D.S.</a></i> (2010) and <i><a href="/wiki/Best_Day_Ever_(mixtape)" title="Best Day Ever (mixtape)">Best Day Ever</a></i> (2011). Miller's debut studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Blue_Slide_Park" title="Blue Slide Park">Blue Slide Park</a></i> (2011), became the first independently distributed debut album to top the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> since 1995.
</p><p>In 2013, he founded the record label imprint REMember Music. After his second studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Watching_Movies_with_the_Sound_Off" title="Watching Movies with the Sound Off">Watching Movies with the Sound Off</a></i> (2013), he left Rostrum and signed with the major label <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Warner Bros. Records">Warner Bros. Records</a> in 2014. With them, he released four studio albums: <i><a href="/wiki/GO:OD_AM" title="GO:OD AM">GO:OD AM</a></i> (2015), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Divine_Feminine" title="The Divine Feminine">The Divine Feminine</a></i> (2016), <i><a href="/wiki/Swimming_(Mac_Miller_album)" title="Swimming (Mac Miller album)">Swimming</a></i> (2018), and the posthumous <i><a href="/wiki/Circles_(Mac_Miller_album)" title="Circles (Mac Miller album)">Circles</a></i> (2020). For <i>Swimming</i>, he was posthumously nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Album">Grammy Award for Best Rap Album</a>. He also served as a record producer for various artists, including himself, under the pseudonym <b>Larry Fisherman</b>.
</p><p>Miller struggled with addiction and <a href="/wiki/Substance_abuse" title="Substance abuse">substance abuse</a>, which was often referenced in his lyrics.<sup id="cite_ref-ET_drugs_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ET_drugs-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> On September 7, 2018, Miller died from an accidental drug overdose of <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fentanyl" title="Fentanyl">fentanyl</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_(drug)" title="Alcohol (drug)">alcohol</a> at his home, at the age of 26.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_and_career">Life and career</span></h2>
<h3><span id="1992.E2.80.932010:_Early_life_and_career_beginnings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1992–2010:_Early_life_and_career_beginnings">1992–2010: Early life and career beginnings</span></h3>
<p>Malcolm James McCormick was born on January 19, 1992,<sup id="cite_ref-Grantland_2015_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grantland_2015-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/Point_Breeze,_Pittsburgh" title="Point Breeze, Pittsburgh">Point Breeze</a> neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_cover_2011_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_cover_2011-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> He was a son of Karen Meyers, a photographer, and Mark McCormick, an architect,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and had an older brother, Miller.<sup id="cite_ref-Rolling_Stone_Last_Days_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Stone_Last_Days-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> His mother is Jewish, and his father is <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DXnext_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DXnext-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> While he and his brother were raised Jewish,<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_cover_2011_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_cover_2011-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mac_talks_heritage_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mac_talks_heritage-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> he attended a <a href="/wiki/Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic">Catholic</a> grade school to "ensure a good education and a chance to play <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse" title="Lacrosse">lacrosse</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_cover_2011_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_cover_2011-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> He later went to <a href="/wiki/Winchester_Thurston_School" title="Winchester Thurston School">Winchester Thurston School</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and graduated from <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Allderdice_High_School" title="Taylor Allderdice High School">Taylor Allderdice High School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pittsburgh_City_Paper_2011_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pittsburgh_City_Paper_2011-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A self-taught musician, Miller played piano, guitar, drums, and bass by the age of six.<sup id="cite_ref-Pittsburgh_City_Paper_2011_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pittsburgh_City_Paper_2011-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-post-gazette_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-post-gazette-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He first started rapping at the age of 14.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Before that, he wanted to be a singer.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In high school, he decided to focus on his rap career, later noting, "Once I hit 15, I got real serious about it and it changed my life completely ... I used to be into sports, play all the sports, go to all the high school parties. But once I found out hip-hop is almost like a job, that's all I did."<sup id="cite_ref-post-gazette_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-post-gazette-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He originally went by the name Easy Mac (often stylized as EZ Mac) and released the <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtape</a> <i>But My Mackin' Ain't Easy</i> in 2007 at the age of 15.<sup id="cite_ref-Grantland_2015_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grantland_2015-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> By 2009, he established himself as Mac Miller, and released two mixtapes: <i>The Jukebox: Prelude to Class Clown</i> and <i>The High Life</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Grantland_2015_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grantland_2015-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> At the 2010 Pittsburgh Hip Hop Awards, Miller won 21 &amp; Under of the Year, and Best Hip Hop Video for "Live Free".<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2010.E2.80.932013:_Breakthrough.2C_Blue_Slide_Park_and_Watching_Movies_with_the_Sound_Off"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010–2013:_Breakthrough,_Blue_Slide_Park_and_Watching_Movies_with_the_Sound_Off">2010–2013: Breakthrough, <i>Blue Slide Park</i> and <i>Watching Movies with the Sound Off</i></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mac_Miller_Governors_Ball_2011.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Mac_Miller_Governors_Ball_2011.jpg/170px-Mac_Miller_Governors_Ball_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Mac_Miller_Governors_Ball_2011.jpg/255px-Mac_Miller_Governors_Ball_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Mac_Miller_Governors_Ball_2011.jpg/340px-Mac_Miller_Governors_Ball_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="5184" /></a><figcaption>Miller performing at the NYC Governor's Ball in 2011</figcaption></figure>
<p>Miller signed with the independent label <a href="/wiki/Rostrum_Records" title="Rostrum Records">Rostrum Records</a> in July 2010, in the lead-up to his mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/K.I.D.S._(album)" class="mw-redirect" title="K.I.D.S. (album)">K.I.D.S.</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Rostrum president Benjy Grinberg met Miller while recording with <a href="/wiki/Wiz_Khalifa" title="Wiz Khalifa">Wiz Khalifa</a> at <a href="/wiki/ID_Labs" title="ID Labs">ID Labs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HitQuarters_interview_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HitQuarters_interview-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Although Grinberg started giving Miller advice, he did not show interest in getting involved with his career until Miller began work on <i>K.I.D.S.</i>, when he "noticed a maturation in his sound and approach to his music".<sup id="cite_ref-HitQuarters_interview_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HitQuarters_interview-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> By that point, Miller had started attracting interest from other record companies, but chose Rostrum due to its location in his hometown and association with Wiz Khalifa.<sup id="cite_ref-HitQuarters_interview_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HitQuarters_interview-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> <i>K.I.D.S.</i> was released by Rostrum in August 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-post-gazette_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-post-gazette-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> During this time, Miller broke through with a focus on social media engagement, digital sales, and persistent touring, due to a lack of radio airplay or mainstream <a href="/wiki/Guest_appearances" class="mw-redirect" title="Guest appearances">features</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/XXL_(magazine)" title="XXL (magazine)">XXL</a></i> featured Miller in its annual <a href="/wiki/XXL_Freshman" class="mw-redirect" title="XXL Freshman">"Freshman Class" list</a> of 2011, alongside 10 other rappers including <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Meek_Mill" title="Meek Mill">Meek Mill</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-xxlmag.com_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxlmag.com-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Miller released his fifth mixtape, <i><a href="/wiki/Best_Day_Ever_(mixtape)" title="Best Day Ever (mixtape)">Best Day Ever</a></i>, in March 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-XXL_Best_Day_Ever_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XXL_Best_Day_Ever-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Its single "<a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump_(song)" title="Donald Trump (song)">Donald Trump</a>" became his first song to chart on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> peaking at number 75,<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_chart_history_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_chart_history-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and received a platinum <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">certification</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA).<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Also in March 2011, he released a six-track <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">EP</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/On_and_On_and_Beyond" title="On and On and Beyond">On and On and Beyond</a></i>. Intended to target a new audience, four of its tracks were previously included on his mixtapes.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The EP was his first entry into the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> albums chart at number 55.<sup id="cite_ref-First_charts_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_charts-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Miller's debut studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Blue_Slide_Park" title="Blue Slide Park">Blue Slide Park</a></i>, released on November 8, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> With 144,000 first week sales, it debuted atop the <i>Billboard</i> 200, the first independently distributed debut album to do so since <a href="/wiki/Tha_Dogg_Pound" title="Tha Dogg Pound">Tha Dogg Pound</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Dogg_Food" title="Dogg Food">Dogg Food</a></i> in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Three songs from the album, "Smile Back", "<a href="/wiki/Frick_Park_Market" title="Frick Park Market">Frick Park Market</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Party_on_Fifth_Ave." title="Party on Fifth Ave.">Party on Fifth Ave.</a>" charted on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, peaking at number 55, 60, and 64, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_chart_history_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_chart_history-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> <i>Blue Slide Park</i> was certified gold in the United States and Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MC_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MC-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Despite its impressive commercial performance, <i>Blue Slide Park</i> received a generally mixed critical response.
</p><p>On March 23, 2012, Miller released his seventh mixtape, <i><a href="/wiki/Macadelic" title="Macadelic">Macadelic</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The single "<a href="/wiki/Loud_(Mac_Miller_song)" title="Loud (Mac Miller song)">Loud</a>" peaked at number 53 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_chart_history_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_chart_history-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In mid-2012, Miller premiered two songs produced by <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell Williams</a>, from a planned collaboration EP, <i>Pink Slime</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_Pink_Slime_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV_Pink_Slime-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> At least ten tracks were completed by August 2012 according to Miller,<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_Pink_Slime_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV_Pink_Slime-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> but the project was not released despite a multi-year effort.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Miller released an EP, <i>You</i>, under the alias Larry Lovestein &amp; The Velvet Revival on November 21, 2012. Rather than rap, the EP features Miller crooning over lounging jazz instrumentals.<sup id="cite_ref-Horowitz2012_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Horowitz2012-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Space_Migration_Tour_London_Music_-_Mac_Miller.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/The_Space_Migration_Tour_London_Music_-_Mac_Miller.jpg/170px-The_Space_Migration_Tour_London_Music_-_Mac_Miller.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="254" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/The_Space_Migration_Tour_London_Music_-_Mac_Miller.jpg/255px-The_Space_Migration_Tour_London_Music_-_Mac_Miller.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/The_Space_Migration_Tour_London_Music_-_Mac_Miller.jpg/340px-The_Space_Migration_Tour_London_Music_-_Mac_Miller.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2746" data-file-height="4096" /></a><figcaption>Miller on <a href="/wiki/The_Space_Migration_Tour" class="mw-redirect" title="The Space Migration Tour">The Space Migration Tour</a> in October 2013</figcaption></figure>
<p>In early 2013, Miller founded the record label imprint REMember Music, named after a deceased friend.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The label primarily focused on Pittsburgh artists, as well as releases for Miller's alter-egos.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Miller starred in a six-episode <a href="/wiki/Reality_series" class="mw-redirect" title="Reality series">reality series</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mac_Miller_and_the_Most_Dope_Family" title="Mac Miller and the Most Dope Family">Mac Miller and the Most Dope Family</a></i>, on <a href="/wiki/MTV2" title="MTV2">MTV2</a>. It followed the production of his upcoming second studio album, and premiered on February 26, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> On March 4, 2013, Miller released a mixtape, <i>Run-On Sentences Vol. 1</i>, solely featuring instrumentals made by himself, under his production alias Larry Fisherman.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Later that month, Miller featured on singer <a href="/wiki/Ariana_Grande" title="Ariana Grande">Ariana Grande</a>'s lead single "<a href="/wiki/The_Way_(Ariana_Grande_song)" title="The Way (Ariana Grande song)">The Way</a>" for her debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Yours_Truly_(Ariana_Grande_album)" title="Yours Truly (Ariana Grande album)">Yours Truly</a></i>;<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> the song is Miller's highest peak on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 at number nine, and was certified triple platinum by the RIAA.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_chart_history_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_chart_history-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>His second studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Watching_Movies_with_the_Sound_Off" title="Watching Movies with the Sound Off">Watching Movies with the Sound Off</a></i>, was released on June 18, 2013. It received generally positive reviews, with most critics praising his new psychedelic sound. The album debuted at number three on the <i>Billboard</i> 200, selling 102,000 copies in its first week.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The album spawned three singles; "<a href="/wiki/S.D.S._(song)" title="S.D.S. (song)">S.D.S.</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Watching_Movies" title="Watching Movies">Watching Movies</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Goosebumpz" title="Goosebumpz">Goosebumpz</a>". The album featured guest appearances from <a href="/wiki/Schoolboy_Q" title="Schoolboy Q">Schoolboy Q</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ab-Soul" title="Ab-Soul">Ab-Soul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Earl_Sweatshirt" title="Earl Sweatshirt">Earl Sweatshirt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tyler,_the_Creator" title="Tyler, the Creator">Tyler, the Creator</a>, <a href="/wiki/Action_Bronson" title="Action Bronson">Action Bronson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jay_Electronica" title="Jay Electronica">Jay Electronica</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-www.hiphopdx.com_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www.hiphopdx.com-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kingofthehill_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kingofthehill-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> According to Miller, the album is "very introspective and very personal so it's kind of throwing it all out there and seeing what happens."<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Pittsburgh mayor <a href="/wiki/Luke_Ravenstahl" title="Luke Ravenstahl">Luke Ravenstahl</a> presented Miller with a <a href="/wiki/Key_to_the_city" class="mw-redirect" title="Key to the city">key to the city</a> on September 20, 2013, and declared the date "Mac Miller Day".<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Vince_Staples" title="Vince Staples">Vince Staples</a>, Miller produced the mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Stolen_Youth_(mixtape)" title="Stolen Youth (mixtape)">Stolen Youth</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Under the moniker Delusional Thomas, Miller self-produced and released an eponymous mixtape, <i><a href="/wiki/Delusional_Thomas" title="Delusional Thomas">Delusional Thomas</a></i>, on October 31, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> On December 17, 2013, Miller released the live album <i><a href="/wiki/Live_from_Space" title="Live from Space">Live from Space</a></i>, containing nine songs performed with the band <a href="/wiki/The_Internet_(band)" title="The Internet (band)">The Internet</a> during his <a href="/wiki/The_Space_Migration_Tour" class="mw-redirect" title="The Space Migration Tour">Space Migration Tour</a> and five studio-recorded tracks that were cut from his second album.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2014.E2.80.932018:_GO:OD_AM.2C_The_Divine_Feminine.2C_and_Swimming"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014–2018:_GO:OD_AM,_The_Divine_Feminine,_and_Swimming">2014–2018: <i>GO:OD AM</i>, <i>The Divine Feminine</i>, and <i>Swimming</i></span></h3>
<p>Miller parted ways with Rostrum Records when his contract expired in January 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> On May 11, 2014, Miller independently released his tenth solo mixtape, <i><a href="/wiki/Faces_(mixtape)" title="Faces (mixtape)">Faces</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_Faces_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Faces-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Colin Stutz of <i>Billboard</i> wrote that the 24-track mixtape "shows [Miller] introspective, ruminating over his drug use, fame and past."<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_Faces_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Faces-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pitchfork (magazine)">Pitchfork</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> Craig Jenkins called <i>Faces</i> his "most consistently honest and personal work to date".<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Miller later reflected on <i>Faces</i>, noting his drug-addled lifestyle while recording it.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The second season of Miller's reality series <i>Mac Miller and the Most Dope Family</i> aired on MTV2 in mid-2014.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2014, Miller signed a recording contract and distribution deal for REMember Music with the major label <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Warner Bros. Records">Warner Bros. Records</a>. He chose Warner as it was "the most independent thinking" company he met with.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Miller's major label debut, <i><a href="/wiki/GO:OD_AM" title="GO:OD AM">GO:OD AM</a></i>, was released on September 18, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> It charted at number four on the <i>Billboard</i> 200, with 87,000 <a href="/wiki/Album-equivalent_unit" title="Album-equivalent unit">album-equivalent units</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The album and the single "<a href="/wiki/Weekend_(Mac_Miller_song)" title="Weekend (Mac Miller song)">Weekend</a>", featuring singer <a href="/wiki/Miguel_(singer)" title="Miguel (singer)">Miguel</a>, were certified gold and platinum by the RIAA, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mac_Miller_(19)_%E2%80%93_splash!_Festival_20_(2017)_(cropped).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Mac_Miller_%2819%29_%E2%80%93_splash%21_Festival_20_%282017%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Mac_Miller_%2819%29_%E2%80%93_splash%21_Festival_20_%282017%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="212" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Mac_Miller_%2819%29_%E2%80%93_splash%21_Festival_20_%282017%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Mac_Miller_%2819%29_%E2%80%93_splash%21_Festival_20_%282017%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Mac_Miller_%2819%29_%E2%80%93_splash%21_Festival_20_%282017%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Mac_Miller_%2819%29_%E2%80%93_splash%21_Festival_20_%282017%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1910" data-file-height="2379" /></a><figcaption>Miller performing at the 2017 <a href="/wiki/Splash!_(festival)" title="Splash! (festival)">Splash! festival</a> in Germany</figcaption></figure>
<p>Miller began work on his next studio album immediately after completing <i>GO:OD AM</i>, wanting to explore the emotion of love.<sup id="cite_ref-Vogue_2016_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vogue_2016-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_Divine_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Divine-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> His fourth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Divine_Feminine" title="The Divine Feminine">The Divine Feminine</a></i>, was released on September 16, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-Complex_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Complex-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The album features Miller singing nearly as much as rapping, and incorporates genres such as <a href="/wiki/R%26B" class="mw-redirect" title="R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Funk" title="Funk">funk</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_Divine_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Divine-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> It received positive reviews, with <i>Pitchfork</i> stating that the album was succinct and refined in its portrayal of love, consequently accentuating Miller's artistry.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Divine Feminine</i> debuted at number two on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and number one on <i>Billboard</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> <a href="/wiki/Top_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Albums" title="Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums">Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums</a> chart with 48,000 units.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Miller's fifth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Swimming_(Mac_Miller_album)" title="Swimming (Mac Miller album)">Swimming</a></i>, was released on August 3, 2018, to positive reviews from critics.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> <i>Pitchfork</i> described the album as consisting of "wistful soul and warm funk", through his exploration of heartbreak and his own mental health issues.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> <i>Swimming</i> debuted at number three on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 with 66,000 units, his fifth consecutive top five-charting album release in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Miller's final public performances included an <a href="/wiki/NPR" title="NPR">NPR</a> <a href="/wiki/Tiny_Desk_Concert" class="mw-redirect" title="Tiny Desk Concert">Tiny Desk Concert</a> released August 6, 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> and a small promotional performance at <a href="/wiki/Hotel_Caf%C3%A9" title="Hotel Café">Hotel Cafe</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hollywood,_Los_Angeles" title="Hollywood, Los Angeles">Hollywood</a> on September 3, 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> both in support of <i>Swimming.</i> After <a href="#Death">his death</a> in September 2018, the single "<a href="/wiki/Self_Care_(song)" title="Self Care (song)">Self Care</a>" rose to number 33 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, his highest peak as a lead artist at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> <i>Swimming</i> was nominated for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Album">Best Rap Album</a> at the <a href="/wiki/61st_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="61st Annual Grammy Awards">61st Annual Grammy Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Posthumous_releases">Posthumous releases</span></h3>
<p>Miller's estate began approving posthumous music releases in June 2019, with the collaborative singles "<a href="/wiki/Time_(Free_Nationals,_Mac_Miller_and_Kali_Uchis_song)" title="Time (Free Nationals, Mac Miller and Kali Uchis song)">Time</a>" with Free Nationals and <a href="/wiki/Kali_Uchis" title="Kali Uchis">Kali Uchis</a>, and "<a href="/wiki/That%27s_Life_(88-Keys_song)" title="That&#39;s Life (88-Keys song)">That's Life</a>" with <a href="/wiki/88-Keys" title="88-Keys">88-Keys</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sia" title="Sia">Sia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> On January 8, 2020, Miller's family announced his first posthumous album, <i><a href="/wiki/Circles_(Mac_Miller_album)" title="Circles (Mac Miller album)">Circles</a></i>, which was released later that month on January 17. Before his death, Miller had been working on the album as a companion album to <i>Swimming</i>. Production was completed by <a href="/wiki/Jon_Brion" title="Jon Brion">Jon Brion</a>, who worked with Miller on both albums.<sup id="cite_ref-Circles_announcement_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Circles_announcement-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> <i>Circles</i> debuted at number three on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 with 164,000 units, his biggest week for an album.<sup id="cite_ref-Circles_BB200_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Circles_BB200-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Its single, "<a href="/wiki/Good_News_(Mac_Miller_song)" title="Good News (Mac Miller song)">Good News</a>", became his highest-charting song as lead artist, peaking at number 17 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_chart_history_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_chart_history-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 29, 2020, his 2010 mixtape <i>K.I.D.S</i> was commercially re-released, followed by a deluxe version on August 13 to celebrate its tenth anniversary, including two previously unreleased songs — "Ayye" and "Back in the Day".<sup id="cite_ref-Deluxe_edition_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deluxe_edition-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Similarly, on October 15, 2021, his 2014 mixtape <i>Faces</i> was also re-released, more than seven years after its initial release.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The re-release of his 2011 mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/I_Love_Life,_Thank_You" title="I Love Life, Thank You">I Love Life, Thank You</a></i> occurred on July 22, 2022. Jazz pianist <a href="/wiki/Robert_Glasper" title="Robert Glasper">Robert Glasper</a> released "Therapy Pt. 2", a song featuring Miller's vocals, in October 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 28, 2023, hip-hop producer <a href="/wiki/Madlib" title="Madlib">Madlib</a> announced via an interview with Sway Universe that he was finishing an album him and Miller were working on years before his passing, whilst confirming that Miller's estate has given clearance for him to release it.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><br />
In August 2023, <a href="/wiki/Ariana_Grande" title="Ariana Grande">Ariana Grande</a> marked the 10th anniversary of her debut album by launching a special edition of her 2013 popular track "<a href="/wiki/The_Way" class="mw-disambig" title="The Way">The Way</a>." This fresh rendition, titled "Live from London," includes the initial vocals of her song's collaborator, Mac Miller. Notably, Miller's vocals intertwine with Ariana Grande's as she performs the song. This holds significance as Grande performs the song live, both with and without Miller's vocals (Grande sometimes performed the song without Mac Miller's vocals before his death) for the first time since Miller's unfortunate passing in 2018.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artistry">Artistry</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_style_and_progression">Musical style and progression</span></h3>
<p>Early in his career, Miller's music was widely regarded as "<a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities">frat</a> rap", with lyrics focusing on partying, smoking <a href="/wiki/Marijuana" class="mw-redirect" title="Marijuana">marijuana</a>, and lusting after fame, money, and women.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-remaking_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-remaking-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> After the mixed critical response of <i>Blue Slide Park</i>, Miller began to employ a more expressive and experimental approach to his subsequent releases.<sup id="cite_ref-remaking_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-remaking-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Miller experimented with <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a> in his career as well. In 2012, Miller released <i>You</i>, an EP featuring <a href="/wiki/Lounge_music" title="Lounge music">lounge-jazz</a> tracks as Larry Lovestein and the Velvet Revival.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Speaking about the Larry Lovestein persona, Miller stated "I've kinda have always had this random fantasy of being a seventy-year-old Lounge Jazz singer."<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Toward the latter half of Miller's career, his music further implemented elements of <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a> and additionally branched to <a href="/wiki/Funk" title="Funk">funk</a> and <a href="/wiki/R%26B" class="mw-redirect" title="R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> <i>Faces</i> incorporated jazz,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> while <i>The Divine Feminine</i> and <i>Swimming</i> have both been described by music publications as <a href="/wiki/Jazz_rap" title="Jazz rap">jazz rap</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Schwartz2020_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schwartz2020-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> writer Danny Schwartz also described <i>Swimming</i> as "spanning rap, funk, and trip-hop."<sup id="cite_ref-Schwartz2020_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schwartz2020-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">Influences</span></h3>
<p>Miller included <a href="/wiki/Big_L" title="Big L">Big L</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lauryn_Hill" title="Lauryn Hill">Lauryn Hill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beastie_Boys" title="Beastie Boys">Beastie Boys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Outkast" title="Outkast">Outkast</a>, and <a href="/wiki/A_Tribe_Called_Quest" title="A Tribe Called Quest">A Tribe Called Quest</a> among his influences.<sup id="cite_ref-rostrum_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rostrum-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> He had a close relationship with fellow Pittsburgh rapper <a href="/wiki/Wiz_Khalifa" title="Wiz Khalifa">Wiz Khalifa</a>, saying "Wiz has been a big brother to me with this music thing so far. Our relationship is beyond music. He really is just my homie, whether I will be making music or not."<sup id="cite_ref-DXnext_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DXnext-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Miller also expressed admiration for <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon" title="John Lennon">John Lennon</a>, he claimed that his background to his iPhone was of Lennon and that he had been a John Lennon fan for a "Long, long, long time".<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Miller also had multiple tattoos of Lennon, including a tattoo of Lennon's face and a tattoo of John Lennon's song "<a href="/wiki/Imagine_(John_Lennon_song)" title="Imagine (John Lennon song)">Imagine</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>Miller spoke openly about his struggle with <a href="/wiki/Substance_abuse" title="Substance abuse">substance abuse</a> and depression.<sup id="cite_ref-ET_drugs_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ET_drugs-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> To manage <a href="/wiki/Stress_(biology)" title="Stress (biology)">stress</a> during his Macadelic Tour in 2012, Miller began taking <a href="/wiki/Promethazine" title="Promethazine">promethazine</a>, and later became addicted to <a href="/wiki/Purple_drank" class="mw-redirect" title="Purple drank">lean</a>. Miller told <i><a href="/wiki/Complex_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Complex (magazine)">Complex</a></i> in January 2013: "I love lean; it's great. I was not happy and I was on lean very heavy. I was so fucked up all the time it was bad. My friends couldn't even look at me the same. I was lost."<sup id="cite_ref-kingofthehill_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kingofthehill-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> He quit taking promethazine in November 2012, before shooting his reality show <i>Mac Miller and the Most Dope Family</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-kingofthehill_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kingofthehill-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, Miller was taking drugs daily, and felt that the final track on <i>Faces</i>, "Grand Finale", was "supposed to be the last song [he] made on Earth." Recounting that period to <i>Billboard</i> in August 2015, Miller was "definitely way healthier" but not "completely" sober.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_Aug_2015_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Aug_2015-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> After stating he "hated" being sober in a February 2016 documentary,<sup id="cite_ref-ET_drugs_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ET_drugs-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Miller had become sober for three months by October 2016, noting his better mood and maintained creativity.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> However, when asked about his sobriety in April 2017, Miller said he was now "living regularly".<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Miller was in an on-again, off-again relationship with writer Nomi Leasure, whom he met in middle school, for seven years until 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_Aug_2015_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Aug_2015-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fader_Jun_2013_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fader_Jun_2013-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Many of the songs on his mixtape <i>Macadelic</i> were about their relationship.<sup id="cite_ref-Fader_Jun_2013_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fader_Jun_2013-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Miller dated singer <a href="/wiki/Ariana_Grande" title="Ariana Grande">Ariana Grande</a> from August 2016 to May 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_issues">Legal issues</span></h3>
<p>In February 2011, while on tour in <a href="/wiki/Upstate_New_York" title="Upstate New York">Upstate New York</a>, Miller and his friends were arrested for <a href="/wiki/Drug_possession" class="mw-redirect" title="Drug possession">possession of marijuana</a> for which they spent the night in jail. Miller said the case was "settled".<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Producer <a href="/wiki/Lord_Finesse" title="Lord Finesse">Lord Finesse</a> filed a $10 million lawsuit against Miller, Rostrum Records and <a href="/wiki/DatPiff" title="DatPiff">DatPiff</a> in July 2012, for the use of a sample of Finesse's song "Hip 2 Da Game" in Miller's 2010 mixtape song "Kool-Aid and Frozen Pizza".<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> In December 2012, the lawsuit was <a href="/wiki/Settlement_(litigation)" title="Settlement (litigation)">settled out of court</a> with its stipulations kept confidential.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2015, the band Aquarian Dream filed a $150,000 lawsuit against Miller for sampling their song "Yesterday (Was So Nice Today)" in the song "Therapy" that appeared on Miller's 2014 mixtape "Faces".<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Miller was arrested in May 2018 on charges of <a href="/wiki/Driving_under_the_influence" title="Driving under the influence">driving under the influence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hit_and_run" title="Hit and run">hit and run</a> after crashing into a utility pole and fleeing the scene with two passengers. Police obtained his address from his license plate number and Miller confessed when police arrived at his home. He was taken into custody and released on $15,000 bail.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> In August 2018, Miller was charged with two counts of driving under the influence for the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Miller died before his arraignment and the charges were dropped.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"><table class="infobox vevent"><caption class="infobox-title summary">Death of Mac Miller</caption><tbody><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Date</th><td class="infobox-data" style="text-align: left;">September&#160;7, 2018<span class="noprint">&#59;&#32;5 years ago</span><span style="display:none">&#160;(<span class="bday dtstart published updated">2018-09-07</span>)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Time</th><td class="infobox-data" style="text-align: left;">11:51 <a href="/wiki/12-hour_clock" title="12-hour clock">a.m.</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pacific_Time_Zone" title="Pacific Time Zone">PST</a>)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Location</th><td class="infobox-data location" style="text-align: left;"><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, U.S.</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Type</th><td class="infobox-data" style="text-align: left;">Accidental <a href="/wiki/Drug_overdose" title="Drug overdose">drug overdose</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Deaths</th><td class="infobox-data" style="text-align: left;">1 (Malcolm James McCormick, <abbr title="also known as">a.k.a.</abbr>&#160;Mac Miller, aged 26)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Accused</th><td class="infobox-data" style="text-align: left;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1126788409">.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul{line-height:inherit;list-style:none;margin:0;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol li,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul li{margin-bottom:0}</style><div class="plainlist">
<ul><li>Cameron James Pettit</li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Convicted</th><td class="infobox-data" style="text-align: left;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1126788409"><div class="plainlist">
<ul><li>Ryan Michael Reavis</li>
<li>Stephen Andrew Walter</li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Charges</th><td class="infobox-data" style="text-align: left;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_(criminal)" class="mw-redirect" title="Conspiracy (criminal)">Conspiring</a> to <a href="/wiki/Illegal_drug_trade_in_the_United_States" title="Illegal drug trade in the United States">distribute controlled substances</a> resulting in death</li>
<li>Distribution of <a href="/wiki/Fentanyl" title="Fentanyl">fentanyl</a> resulting in death<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Verdict</th><td class="infobox-data" style="text-align: left;"><b>Reavis and Walter:</b><br /><a href="/wiki/Pleaded_guilty" class="mw-redirect" title="Pleaded guilty">Pleaded guilty</a> to distribution of fentanyl<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Sentence</th><td class="infobox-data" style="text-align: left;"><b>Reavis:</b><br />10 years and 11 months in prison<br /><b>Walter:</b><br /><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1154941027">.mw-parser-output .frac{white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output .frac .num,.mw-parser-output .frac .den{font-size:80%;line-height:0;vertical-align:super}.mw-parser-output .frac .den{vertical-align:sub}.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);clip-path:polygon(0px 0px,0px 0px,0px 0px);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px}</style><span class="frac" role="math">17<span class="sr-only">+</span><span class="num">1</span>&#8260;<span class="den">2</span></span> years in prison<sup id="cite_ref-npr.org_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-npr.org-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>On September 7, 2018, Miller was found unresponsive in his <a href="/wiki/Studio_City,_Los_Angeles" title="Studio City, Los Angeles">Studio City</a> home by his personal assistant, who called <a href="/wiki/9-1-1" title="9-1-1">911</a> and performed <a href="/wiki/CPR" class="mw-redirect" title="CPR">CPR</a> until paramedics arrived. Miller was pronounced dead at the scene at 11:51&#160;a.m. (<a href="/wiki/Pacific_Time_Zone" title="Pacific Time Zone">PDT</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> He had been scheduled to shoot a music video on the day of his death, and was to embark on his <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(Mac_Miller_album)#Release_and_promotion" title="Swimming (Mac Miller album)">Swimming Tour</a> in October.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> In his will, Miller named his mother, father, and brother as beneficiaries.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> He was buried at <a href="/wiki/Homewood_Cemetery" title="Homewood Cemetery">Homewood Cemetery</a> in his hometown of Pittsburgh, in a Jewish funeral.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> On November 5, 2018, the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County_Coroner" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles County Coroner">Los Angeles County Coroner</a>'s office determined that Miller died from an accidental drug overdose due to a "mixed drug toxicity" of <a href="/wiki/Fentanyl" title="Fentanyl">fentanyl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_(drug)" title="Alcohol (drug)">alcohol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cause_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cause-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Thousands of fans held a vigil for Miller on September 11, 2018, at Pittsburgh's <a href="/wiki/Frick_Park" title="Frick Park">Blue Slide Park</a>, the inspiration behind his debut album title;<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> the site continues to be a place of remembrance.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> A tribute concert, Mac Miller: A Celebration of Life, took place on October 31, 2018, at the <a href="/wiki/Greek_Theatre_(Los_Angeles)" title="Greek Theatre (Los Angeles)">Greek Theatre</a> in Los Angeles. Many of his friends and collaborators performed or provided messages at the concert; proceeds raised benefited the newly established Mac Miller Circles Fund, which aims to support youth arts and community-building programs in his memory.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> The charity had raised over $700,000 by January 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> In May 2019, the renamed Mac Miller Fund issued its first grants, including $50,000 to <a href="/wiki/MusiCares" title="MusiCares">MusiCares</a>, which was used to launch their Mac Miller Legacy Fund to help young musicians with substance abuse issues.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Three men were arrested in September 2019 during an investigation into Miller's death. Cameron James Pettit allegedly sold Miller counterfeit <a href="/wiki/Oxycodone" title="Oxycodone">oxycodone</a> pills containing fentanyl two days before his death, which were run to Pettit by Ryan Reavis and supplied by Stephen Walter. Miller had asked Pettit for <a href="/wiki/Percocet" class="mw-redirect" title="Percocet">Percocet</a>, a prescribed painkiller containing oxycodone, in addition to cocaine and <a href="/wiki/Xanax" class="mw-redirect" title="Xanax">Xanax</a>. Investigators believe Miller snorted the laced pills before his death.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> The three men were indicted on charges of conspiracy and distribution of drugs resulting in death.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 18, 2022, Reavis was sentenced to ten years in prison for his role in distributing the pills.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> On May 17, 2022, Walter was sentenced to <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1154941027"><span class="frac" role="math">17<span class="sr-only">+</span><span class="num">1</span>&#8260;<span class="den">2</span></span> years in prison for his role.<sup id="cite_ref-npr.org_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-npr.org-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span></h2>
